margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1">The governorship is an administrative post appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Finland" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Finland">Government of Finland</a> and does not have any authority over the autonomous <a href="/wiki/Government_of_%C3%85land" title="Government of \xc3\x85land">Government of \xc3\x85land</a>.</li><li value="2">Settled by the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> following the <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_Islands_dispute" title="\xc3\x85land Islands dispute">\xc3\x85land Islands dispute</a>.</li><li value="3">\xc3\x85land held a separate referendum and then <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_their_relations_with_the_European_Union#\xc3\x85land_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Special member state territories and their relations with the European Union">joined at the same time</a> as the rest of Finland.</li><li value="4">Until 1999, the <a href="/wiki/Finnish_markka" title="Finnish markka">Finnish markka</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Swedish_krona" title="Swedish krona">Swedish krona</a> (SEK) is also widely used.</li><li value="5"><a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbers_in_%C3%85land" title="Telephone numbers in \xc3\x85land">Area code 18</a>.</li><li value="6">Replacing .aland.fi from August 2006. The <a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, as it is shared with Finland and the rest of <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>\xc3\x85land Islands</b> or <b>\xc3\x85land</b> (<a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">\xc3\x85land</i>, <small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Swedish" title="Help:IPA/Swedish">[\xcb\x88o\xcb\x90land]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>: <i lang="fi">Ahvenanmaa</i>) is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> <a href="/wiki/Province" title="Province">province</a> at the entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Bothnia" title="Gulf of Bothnia">Gulf of Bothnia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> belonging to <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>. It is <a href="/wiki/Federacy" title="Federacy">autonomous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demilitarized_zone" title="Demilitarized zone">demilitarised</a> and is the only <a href="/wiki/Monolingualism" title="Monolingualism">monolingually</a> <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish-speaking</a> region in Finland. It is the smallest <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Finland" title="Regions of Finland">region of Finland</a>, constituting 0.49% of its land area and 0.50% of its population.\n</p><p>\xc3\x85land comprises <a href="/wiki/Fasta_%C3%85land" title="Fasta \xc3\x85land">Fasta \xc3\x85land</a> on which 90% of the population resides<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and a further 6,500 <a href="/wiki/Skerry" title="Skerry">skerries</a> and islands to its east.<sup id="cite_ref-readersnatural_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-readersnatural-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Fasta \xc3\x85land is separated from the coast of <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> by 38 kilometres (24&#160;mi) of open water to the west. In the east, the \xc3\x85land archipelago is <a href="/wiki/Geographic_contiguity" title="Geographic contiguity">contiguous</a> with the Finnish <a href="/wiki/Archipelago_Sea" title="Archipelago Sea">Archipelago Sea</a>. \xc3\x85land\'s only land border is located on the uninhabited skerry of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A4rket" title="M\xc3\xa4rket">M\xc3\xa4rket</a>, which it shares with Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\xc3\x85land\'s autonomous status means that those provincial powers normally exercised by representatives of the central Finnish government are largely exercised by <a href="/wiki/Government_of_%C3%85land" title="Government of \xc3\x85land">its own government</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Autonomy"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Autonomy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Etymology"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Administration"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Administration</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Municipalities"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Municipalities</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Geography"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Geography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Economy"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Economy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Demographics"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Demographics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Immigration"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Immigration</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Births_and_deaths"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Births and deaths</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Ethnicity_and_language"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Ethnicity and language</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Religion"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">11.3</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomy">Autonomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Autonomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">Special member state territories and the European Union</a></div>\n<p>The autonomous status of the islands was affirmed by a decision made by the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a> in 1921 following the <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_Islands_dispute" title="\xc3\x85land Islands dispute">\xc3\x85land Islands dispute</a>. It was reaffirmed within the treaty admitting Finland to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. By law, \xc3\x85land is politically neutral and entirely demilitarised, and residents are exempt from <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Defence_Forces" title="Finnish Defence Forces">Finnish Defence Forces</a>. The islands were granted extensive autonomy by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland" title="Parliament of Finland">Parliament of Finland</a> in the Act on the Autonomy of \xc3\x85land of 1920, which was later replaced by new legislation by the same name in 1951 and 1991. The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Finland" title="Constitution of Finland">constitution of Finland</a> defines a "<a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_%C3%85land" title="Constitution of \xc3\x85land">constitution of \xc3\x85land</a>" by referring to this act. \xc3\x85land remains exclusively Swedish-speaking by this act.<sup id="cite_ref-FINLEX_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FINLEX-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In connection with Finland\'s admission to the European Union, a protocol was signed concerning the \xc3\x85land Islands that stipulates, among other things, that provisions of the <a href="/wiki/European_Community_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community Treaty">European Community Treaty</a> shall not force a change of the existing restrictions for foreigners (i.e., persons who do not enjoy "home region rights"\xe2\x80\x94<i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">hembygdsr\xc3\xa4tt</i>\xe2\x80\x94in \xc3\x85land) to acquire and hold real property or to provide certain services.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>\xc3\x85land\'s original name was in the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Norse_language" title="Proto-Norse language">Proto-Norse language</a> *<i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text">Ahvaland</i> which means "land of water". In Swedish, this first developed into <i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">\xc3\x81land</i> and eventually into <i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">\xc3\x85land</i>, literally "river land"\xe2\x80\x94even though rivers are not a prominent feature of \xc3\x85land\'s geography. The <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a> names of the island, <i lang="fi" title="Finnish language text">Ahvenanmaa</i> and <i lang="et" title="Estonian language text">Ahvenamaa</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Perch" title="Perch">perch</a> land"), are seen to preserve another form of the old name.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another theory suggests that the Finnish <i lang="fi" title="Finnish language text">Ahvenanmaa</i> would be the original name of the archipelago, from which the Swedish <i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">\xc3\x85land</i> derives.<sup id="cite_ref-Hulden_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hulden-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The official name, <i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">Landskapet \xc3\x85land</i>, means "the Region of \xc3\x85land"; <i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">landskap</i> is <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognate</a> to English "landscape".\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_%C3%85land_Islands" title="History of the \xc3\x85land Islands">History of the \xc3\x85land Islands</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Geographisch_delineation_%C3%B6ffver_%C3%85landh.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Geographisch_delineation_%C3%B6ffver_%C3%85landh.jpg/220px-Geographisch_delineation_%C3%B6ffver_%C3%85landh.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Geographisch_delineation_%C3%B6ffver_%C3%85landh.jpg/330px-Geographisch_delineation_%C3%B6ffver_%C3%85landh.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Geographisch_delineation_%C3%B6ffver_%C3%85landh.jpg/440px-Geographisch_delineation_%C3%B6ffver_%C3%85landh.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2253" data-file-height="1763" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Geographisch_delineation_%C3%B6ffver_%C3%85landh.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Swedish Map of \xc3\x85land from before 1667 with shipping lanes, harbors, churches and various boundaries marked</div></div></div>\n<p>Members of the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Comb_Ceramic" title="Comb Ceramic">Comb Ceramic</a> culture started settling the islands some 7000 years ago, after the islands had begun to re-emerge from the sea after being pushed down by the weight of the continental ice of the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">latest ice age</a>. Two neolithic cultures met on \xc3\x85land: Comb Ceramic culture and later <a href="/wiki/Pit%E2%80%93Comb_Ware_culture" title="Pit\xe2\x80\x93Comb Ware culture">Pit-Comb Ware culture</a> which spread from the west.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-MUSEUM_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUSEUM-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> people obtained food by hunting seals and birds, fishing, and gathering plants. They also started agriculture early on. In the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>, contacts to Scandinavia were increasing. From the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Viking age</a> there are over 380 documented burial sites and six castle ruins.<sup id="cite_ref-MUSEUM_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MUSEUM-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The \xc3\x85land Islands formed part of the territory ceded to <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a> by <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fredrikshamn" title="Treaty of Fredrikshamn">Treaty of Fredrikshamn</a> in September 1809. As a result, they became part of the semi-<a href="/wiki/Autonomous_entity" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous entity">autonomous</a> <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Finland" title="Grand Duchy of Finland">Grand Duchy of Finland</a>. During this process, Sweden failed to secure a provision that the islands not be fortified. The issue was important not only for Sweden but also for the United Kingdom, which was concerned that a military presence on the islands could threaten Britain\'s military and commercial interests.\n</p><p>In 1832, Russia started to fortify the islands with the great fortress of <a href="/wiki/Bomarsund,_%C3%85land" class="mw-redirect" title="Bomarsund, \xc3\x85land">Bomarsund</a>. A combined British and French force of warships and marines captured and destroyed the fortress in 1854 as part of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_theatre_of_the_Crimean_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Baltic theatre of the Crimean War">campaign in the Baltic</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1856)" title="Treaty of Paris (1856)">1856 Treaty of Paris</a> demilitarised the entire \xc3\x85land archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Civil_War" title="Finnish Civil War">Finnish Civil War</a>, in 1918, <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_%C3%85land#The_Swedish_invasion" title="Invasion of \xc3\x85land">Swedish troops intervened</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> force between the Russian troops stationed on the islands and <a href="/wiki/Whites_(Finland)" title="Whites (Finland)">"White"</a> and <a href="/wiki/Finnish_Socialist_Workers%27_Republic" title="Finnish Socialist Workers&#39; Republic">"Red"</a> Finnish troops who came from Finland over the frozen sea. (Historians<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (July 2015)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> point out that Sweden may have in reality planned to occupy the islands.) Within weeks, the Swedish troops gave way to <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea_Division" title="Baltic Sea Division">German troops</a> who <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_%C3%85land#The_German_invasion" title="Invasion of \xc3\x85land">occupied \xc3\x85land</a> by request of the "White" (conservative) <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Finland" title="Senate of Finland">Senate of Finland</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Historical_province_of_%C3%85land_in_Finland.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Historical_province_of_%C3%85land_in_Finland.png/170px-Historical_province_of_%C3%85land_in_Finland.png" width="170" height="298" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Historical_province_of_%C3%85land_in_Finland.png/255px-Historical_province_of_%C3%85land_in_Finland.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Historical_province_of_%C3%85land_in_Finland.png/340px-Historical_province_of_%C3%85land_in_Finland.png 2x" data-file-width="1957" data-file-height="3429" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Historical_province_of_%C3%85land_in_Finland.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\xc3\x85land (blue) with historical and modern provinces of Finland (yellow) juxtaposed.</div></div></div>\n<p>After 1917 the residents of the islands worked towards having them ceded to Sweden. In 1919 <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_status_referendum,_1919" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x85land status referendum, 1919">a petition</a> for secession from Finland and integration with Sweden was signed by 96.4% of the voters on the islands, with over 95% in favour.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Swedish nationalist sentiments had grown strong particularly as a result of the anti-Swedish tendencies in Finland and Finnish nationalism fueled by Finland\'s struggle to retain its autonomy and resistance against <a href="/wiki/Russification_of_Finland" title="Russification of Finland">Russification</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Finland%27s_language_strife" title="Finland&#39;s language strife">conflict between the Swedish-speaking minority and the Finnish-speaking majority</a> on the mainland, prominent in Finnish politics since the 1840s, contributed to the apprehension of the \xc3\x85land population about its future in Finland.\n</p><p>Finland, however, declined to cede the islands and instead offered them an autonomous status. Nevertheless, the residents did not approve the offer, and the dispute over the islands was submitted to the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>. The latter decided that Finland should retain <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> over the province but that the \xc3\x85land Islands should be made an autonomous territory. Thus Finland was obliged to ensure the residents of the \xc3\x85land Islands the right to maintain the Swedish language, as well as their own culture and local traditions. At the same time, an international treaty established the neutral status of \xc3\x85land, prohibiting the placing of military installations or forces on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-ELGAN_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ELGAN-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The combination of disappointment about insufficient support from Sweden in the League of Nations, Swedish disrespect for \xc3\x85land\'s demilitarised status in the 1930s, and some feelings of a shared destiny with Finland during and after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> has changed the islanders\' perception of \xc3\x85land\'s relation to Finland from "a Swedish province in Finnish possession" to "an autonomous part of Finland".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The islanders enjoyed safety at sea during World War II, as their merchant fleet sailed for both the Allied countries and Germany. Consequently, \xc3\x85land shipping was not generally attacked as each side rarely knew which cargo was being carried to whom.\n</p><p>Finland marked the 150th anniversary of demilitarisation of the \xc3\x85land Islands by issuing a high-value commemorative coin, the \xe2\x82\xac5 <a href="/wiki/Euro_gold_and_silver_commemorative_coins_(Finland)#2006_coinage" title="Euro gold and silver commemorative coins (Finland)">150th Anniversary of Demilitarisation of \xc3\x85land Islands commemorative coin</a>, minted in 2006. The obverse depicts a pine tree, very typical in the \xc3\x85land Islands. The reverse design features a boat\'s stern and rudder, with a dove perched on the tiller, a symbol of 150 years of peace.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_%C3%85land" title="Politics of \xc3\x85land">Politics of \xc3\x85land</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%85lands_lagting.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/%C3%85lands_lagting.jpg/220px-%C3%85lands_lagting.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/%C3%85lands_lagting.jpg/330px-%C3%85lands_lagting.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/%C3%85lands_lagting.jpg/440px-%C3%85lands_lagting.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%C3%85lands_lagting.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_%C3%85land" title="Parliament of \xc3\x85land">Parliament of \xc3\x85land</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alands.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Alands.jpg/220px-Alands.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Alands.jpg/330px-Alands.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/Alands.jpg/440px-Alands.jpg 2x" data-file-width="943" data-file-height="521" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alands.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The \xc3\x85land Islands during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>. It was here that the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bomarsund" title="Battle of Bomarsund">Battle of Bomarsund</a> was fought.</div></div></div>\n<p>The \xc3\x85land Islands are governed according to the Act on the Autonomy of \xc3\x85land and international treaties. These laws guarantee the islands\' autonomy from Finland, which has ultimate sovereignty over them, as well as a demilitarised status. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_%C3%85land" title="Government of \xc3\x85land">Government of \xc3\x85land</a>, or <i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">Landskapsregering</i>, answers to the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_%C3%85land" title="Parliament of \xc3\x85land">Parliament of \xc3\x85land</a>, or <i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">Lagting</i>, in accordance with the principles of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentarism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FINLEX_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FINLEX-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\xc3\x85land has its own flag and has issued its own postage stamps since 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> It runs its own police force, and is an associate member of the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Council" title="Nordic Council">Nordic Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  Since 2005, the \xc3\x85land Islands also have had their own airline, <a href="/wiki/Air_%C3%85land" title="Air \xc3\x85land">Air \xc3\x85land</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  The islands are demilitarised, and the population is exempt from <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a>. Although \xc3\x85land\'s autonomy preceded the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Finland" title="Regions of Finland">regions of Finland</a>, the autonomous government of \xc3\x85land also has responsibility for the functions undertaken by Finland\'s regional councils. <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_Post" title="\xc3\x85land Post">\xc3\x85land Post</a> provides postal services to the islands, and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Small_European_Postal_Administration_Cooperation" title="Small European Postal Administration Cooperation">Small European Postal Administration Cooperation</a>. The islands are considered a separate "nation" for <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">amateur radio</a> purposes and have their own <a href="/wiki/Call_sign" title="Call sign">call sign</a> <a href="/wiki/ITU_prefix" title="ITU prefix">prefix</a> granted by Finland, <code>OH0</code>, <code>OF0</code> and <code>OG0</code> (last character is zero).<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The \xc3\x85land Islands are guaranteed representation in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Finland" title="Parliament of Finland">Finnish parliament</a>, to which they elect one representative. \xc3\x85land also has a different system of political parties from the mainland (see <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Finland" title="List of political parties in Finland">List of political parties in Finland</a>).\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Homeschooling" title="Homeschooling">Homeschooling</a>, which was effectively banned in Sweden in 2011, is allowed by the Finnish government. Due to the islands\' proximity to Sweden and because the islands are Swedish speaking, a number of Swedish homeschooling families have moved from the Swedish mainland to \xc3\x85land, including Jonas Himmelstrand, the chairman of the Swedish association for homeschooling.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration">Administration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Administration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aland_Islands_License_Plate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aland_Islands_License_Plate.jpg/220px-Aland_Islands_License_Plate.jpg" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aland_Islands_License_Plate.jpg/330px-Aland_Islands_License_Plate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Aland_Islands_License_Plate.jpg/440px-Aland_Islands_License_Plate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="662" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aland_Islands_License_Plate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An \xc3\x85land license plate.</div></div></div>\n<p>The State Department of \xc3\x85land represents the Finnish central government and performs many administrative duties. It has a somewhat different function from the other Regional Administrative Agencies, owing to its <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/autonomy" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:autonomy">autonomy</a>. Before 2010, the state administration was handled by the <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_State_Provincial_Office" title="\xc3\x85land State Provincial Office">\xc3\x85land State Provincial Office</a>.\n</p><p>\xc3\x85land has its own postal administration but still uses the Finnish five-digit <a href="/wiki/List_of_postal_codes_in_Finland" title="List of postal codes in Finland">postal code</a> system, using the number range 22000\xe2\x80\x9322999, with the prefix AX. The lowest numbered postal code is for the capital Mariehamn, AX 22100, and the highest AX 22950 for Jurmo.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipalities">Municipalities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Municipalities">edit</a><span href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_%C3%85land" title="Geography of \xc3\x85land">Geography of \xc3\x85land</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_%C3%85land.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Topographic_map_of_%C3%85land.svg/220px-Topographic_map_of_%C3%85land.svg.png" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Topographic_map_of_%C3%85land.svg/330px-Topographic_map_of_%C3%85land.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Topographic_map_of_%C3%85land.svg/440px-Topographic_map_of_%C3%85land.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="681" data-file-height="516" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_%C3%85land.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geographical features and municipalities of the \xc3\x85land Islands.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SoedraLinjen_15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/SoedraLinjen_15.jpg/220px-SoedraLinjen_15.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/SoedraLinjen_15.jpg/330px-SoedraLinjen_15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/SoedraLinjen_15.jpg/440px-SoedraLinjen_15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1136" data-file-height="674" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SoedraLinjen_15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sheep grazing on a small island.</div></div></div>\n<p>The \xc3\x85land Islands occupy a position of strategic importance, as they command one of the entrances to the port of <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>, as well as the approaches to the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Bothnia" title="Gulf of Bothnia">Gulf of Bothnia</a>, in addition to being situated near the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">Gulf of Finland</a>.\n</p><p>The \xc3\x85land archipelago includes nearly three hundred habitable islands, of which about eighty are inhabited; the remainder are merely some 6,200 <a href="/wiki/Skerry" title="Skerry">skerries</a> and desolate rocks.<sup id="cite_ref-readersnatural_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-readersnatural-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The archipelago is connected to <a href="/wiki/%C3%85boland" title="\xc3\x85boland">\xc3\x85boland</a> archipelago in the east (<a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>: <i lang="fi">Turunmaan saaristo</i>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>: <i lang="sv">\xc3\x85bolands sk\xc3\xa4rg\xc3\xa5rd</i>)\xe2\x80\x94the archipelago adjacent to the southwest coast of Finland. Together they form the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago_Sea" title="Archipelago Sea">Archipelago Sea</a>. To the West from \xc3\x85land is the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_%C3%85land" title="Sea of \xc3\x85land">Sea of \xc3\x85land</a> and to the North is the <a href="/wiki/Bothnian_Sea" title="Bothnian Sea">Bothnian Sea</a>.\n</p><p>The surface of the islands is generally rocky and the soil thin due to glacial stripping at the end of the most recent ice age.<sup id="cite_ref-readersnatural_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-readersnatural-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The islands also contain many meadows that are home to many different kinds of insects, such as the <a href="/wiki/Glanville_fritillary" title="Glanville fritillary">Glanville fritillary</a> butterfly. There are several harbours.\n</p><p>The islands\' landmass occupies a total area of 1,527 square kilometres (590&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Statfin_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statfin-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Ninety percent of the population live on <a href="/wiki/Fasta_%C3%85land" title="Fasta \xc3\x85land">Fasta \xc3\x85land</a>, which is also the site of the capital town of <a href="/wiki/Mariehamn" title="Mariehamn">Mariehamn</a>. Fasta \xc3\x85land is the largest island in the archipelago. Its area is difficult to estimate due to its irregular shape and coastline, but estimates range from 740 square kilometres<sup id="cite_ref-readersnatural_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-readersnatural-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> to 879 square kilometres<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> to over 1,010 square kilometres, depending on what is included or excluded.\n</p><p>During the \xc3\x85land Islands dispute, the parties sought support from different maps of the islands. On the Swedish map, the most densely populated main island dominated, and many <a href="/wiki/Skerry" title="Skerry">skerries</a> were left out. On the Finnish map, many smaller islands or skerries were, for technical reasons, given a slightly exaggerated size. The Swedish map made the islands appear to be closer to the mainland of Sweden than to Finland; the Finnish map stressed the continuity of the archipelago between the main island and <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Finland" title="Mainland Finland">mainland Finland</a>, while a greater gap appeared between the islands and the archipelago on the Swedish side. One consequence is the often repeated number of "over 6,000" skerries that was given authority by the outcome of the arbitration.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>\xc3\x85land has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> that is influenced by its maritime position, especially in summer. While summers are cooler than on both the Swedish and Finnish mainland, winters see little difference to the adjacent parts of Sweden and are only narrowly milder than in mainland Finland.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; font-size:95%;">Source &#35;2: M\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9o Climat<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SoedraLinjen_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/SoedraLinjen_05.jpg/220px-SoedraLinjen_05.jpg" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/SoedraLinjen_05.jpg/330px-SoedraLinjen_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/SoedraLinjen_05.jpg/440px-SoedraLinjen_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1273" data-file-height="739" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SoedraLinjen_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ferry port in <a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%96ver%C3%B6&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="\xc3\x96ver\xc3\xb6 (page does not exist)">\xc3\x96ver\xc3\xb6</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://sv.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%96ver%C3%B6" class="extiw" title="sv:\xc3\x96ver\xc3\xb6">sv</a>)</span>, <a href="/wiki/F%C3%B6gl%C3%B6" title="F\xc3\xb6gl\xc3\xb6">F\xc3\xb6gl\xc3\xb6</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>\xc3\x85land\'s economy is heavily dominated by shipping, trade and <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_%C3%85land" title="Tourism in \xc3\x85land">tourism</a>. Shipping represents about 40% of the economy, with several international carriers owned and operated off \xc3\x85land. Most companies aside from shipping are small, with fewer than ten employees. Farming and fishing are important in combination with the food industry. A few high-profile technology companies contribute to a prosperous economy. Wind power is rapidly developing, aiming at reversing the direction in the cables to the mainland in coming years. In December 2011, wind power accounted for 31.5% of \xc3\x85land\'s total electricity usage.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The main ports are <a href="/wiki/Mariehamn" title="Mariehamn">Mariehamn</a> (south), <a href="/wiki/Berghamn_(%C3%85land)" title="Berghamn (\xc3\x85land)">Berghamn</a> (west) and <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A5ngn%C3%A4s" title="L\xc3\xa5ngn\xc3\xa4s">L\xc3\xa5ngn\xc3\xa4s</a> on the eastern shore of the Main Island.\n</p><p>Mariehamn served as the base for the last large oceanic commercial sailing-ships in the world. Their final tasks involved bringing Australian wheat to Great Britain, a trade which \xc3\x85land shipowner <a href="/wiki/Gustaf_Erikson" title="Gustaf Erikson">Gustaf Erikson</a> kept going until 1947. The ships latterly made only one round-trip from South Australia to Britain per year, (the <a href="/wiki/Grain_race" title="Grain race">grain race</a>), after each marathon voyage going back to Mariehamn to lay up for a few months. The ship <a href="/wiki/Pommern_(ship)" title="Pommern (ship)"> <i>Pommern</i></a>, now a museum in Mariehamn, was one of these last vessels.\n</p><p>The abolition of tax-free sales on ferry boats travelling between destinations within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> made Finland demand an exception for the \xc3\x85land Islands on the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_value_added_tax#EU_VAT_area" title="European Union value added tax">European Union value-added tax rules</a>. The exception allows for maintained tax-free sales on the ferries between Sweden and Finland (provided they stop at Mariehamn or L\xc3\xa5ngn\xc3\xa4s) and at <a href="/wiki/Mariehamn_Airport" title="Mariehamn Airport">the airport</a>, but has also made \xc3\x85land a different tax-zone, meaning that tariffs must be levied on goods brought to the islands.\n</p><p>Unemployment was 3.9% in January 2014<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Finnish State also collects taxes, duties and fees in \xc3\x85land. In return, the Finnish Government places a sum of money at the disposal of the \xc3\x85land Parliament. The sum is 0.5% of total Government income, excluding Government loans. If the sum paid to the Finnish state exceeds 0.5%, then any amount above goes back to the Parliament of \xc3\x85land as "diligence money".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 2010 the amount of taxes paid by \xc3\x85land Islanders comprised 0.7% of the total taxes paid in Finland.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, as of  2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> \xc3\x85land was the 20th-wealthiest of the EU\'s 268 regions, and the wealthiest in Finland, with a GDP per inhabitant 47% above the EU mean.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>While the official currency is the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a>, most <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">businesses</a> in \xc3\x85land unofficially accept the <a href="/wiki/Swedish_krona" title="Swedish krona">Swedish krona</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bauernhochzeit_Jomala_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Bauernhochzeit_Jomala_1.jpg/220px-Bauernhochzeit_Jomala_1.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bauernhochzeit_Jomala_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A mock wedding in <a href="/wiki/Jomala" title="Jomala">Jomala</a>. This event, a reenactment of an 1800s farmer\'s wedding (<i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">bondbr\xc3\xb6llop</i>) is held annually, mostly as a tourist attraction.</div></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity_and_language">Ethnicity and language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ethnicity and language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_%C3%85land" title="Languages of \xc3\x85land">Languages of \xc3\x85land</a></div>\n<p>Most inhabitants speak <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> (the sole <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a>) as their <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a>: 90.2% in 2009, while 5.0% spoke <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>. The language of instruction in publicly financed schools is Swedish (In the rest of Finland, bilingual municipalities provide schooling both in Finnish and in Swedish). (See <a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_Swedish" title="\xc3\x85land Swedish">\xc3\x85land Swedish</a> for information about the dialect.)\n</p><p>The issue of the ethnicity of the \xc3\x85landers, and the correct linguistic classification of their language, remains somewhat sensitive and controversial. They may be considered either ethnic <a href="/wiki/Swedes" title="Swedes">Swedes</a> or <a href="/wiki/Swedish-speaking_population_of_Finland" title="Swedish-speaking population of Finland">Swedish-speaking Finns</a>, but their language is closer to the <a href="/wiki/Uppl%C3%A4ndska_dialect" title="Uppl\xc3\xa4ndska dialect">Uppl\xc3\xa4ndska dialect</a> of Sweden than to <a href="/wiki/Finland_Swedish" title="Finland Swedish">Finland Swedish</a>. See <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Sweden" title="Languages of Sweden">Languages of Sweden</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Finnish_nationality_law#\xc3\x85landic_provincial_right_of_domicile" title="Finnish nationality law">Regional citizenship or the right of domicile</a> (<i lang="sv" title="Swedish language text">hembygdsr\xc3\xa4tt</i>) is a prerequisite for voting, standing as a candidate for the Legislative Assembly, or owning and holding real estate situated in unplanned areas of \xc3\x85land.<sup id="cite_ref-FINLEX_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FINLEX-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jomala_church_2_retouched.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Jomala_church_2_retouched.jpg/220px-Jomala_church_2_retouched.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Jomala_church_2_retouched.jpg/330px-Jomala_church_2_retouched.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Jomala_church_2_retouched.jpg/440px-Jomala_church_2_retouched.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2616" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jomala_church_2_retouched.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/St._Olaf%27s_Church,_Jomala" title="St. Olaf&#39;s Church, Jomala">St. Olaf\'s Church, Jomala</a>, is the oldest in Finland.</div></div></div>\n<p>The majority of the population, 74.5%, belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_of_Finland" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church of Finland">Evangelical Lutheran Church of Finland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The \xc3\x85land islands contain Finland\'s oldest Christian churches, including <a href="/wiki/St._Olaf%27s_Church,_Jomala" title="St. Olaf&#39;s Church, Jomala">St. Olaf\'s Church, Jomala</a>, which dating from the late 13th century is likely to be the oldest in Finland. The \xc3\x85land Islands\' largest church is the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Church_of_St._George,_Sund&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Church of St. George, Sund (page does not exist)">Church of St. George</a> in  <a href="/wiki/Sund,_%C3%85land" title="Sund, \xc3\x85land">Sund</a>, dating from shortly after.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%85land_Islands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aaland_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Aaland_1.jpg/220px-Aaland_1.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Aaland_1.jpg/330px-Aaland_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/Aaland_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aaland_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The sailing ship <i>Linden</i> (center) in \xc3\x96stra Hamnen, Mariehamn\'s eastern port.</div></div></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_Islands_official_football_team" title="\xc3\x85land Islands official football team">\xc3\x85land</a> competes in the biennial <a href="/wiki/International_Island_Games_Association" title="International Island Games Association">Island Games</a>, which it hosted in 1991 and 2009.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%85land_United" title="\xc3\x85land United">\xc3\x85land United</a> and <a href="/wiki/IFK_Mariehamn" title="IFK Mariehamn">IFK Mariehamn</a> are the islands\' leading football clubs.</li></ul>\n<div style="clear:left;"></div>\n<p>\xc3\x85land Stags is the islands\' only Rugby Union club.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See
